## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: constitutive modeling / thermomechanical materials science
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in solid mechanics. Stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic laws, and temperature modifies material stiffness and flow stress through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Power-law with thermal softening (linear): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (widely used thermomechanical constitutive model)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturation hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear terms)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law for pre-strained materials)
- Swift with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power-law with thermal softening)
- Polynomial thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic thermal modulus variation)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturating stress-strain with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening in metals → Power-law form epsilon**c with exponent typically 0 < c < 1 (concave stress-strain curve)
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) indicating a non-zero stress at zero plastic strain
- Saturation hardening → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c*epsilon)), stress plateaus at large strain
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors reflecting atomic-scale thermal activation
- Separable strain-temperature dependence → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T), common in Johnson-Cook-type models
- Pre-strain or initial dislocation density → Shifted strain argument (epsilon + c0)**c1 rather than pure epsilon**c1
- Phase transformation or anomalous behavior → Non-monotonic temperature dependence, requiring polynomial or peaked T terms like T*exp(-c*T)
